tags:
  - empathegy
  - witness
  - protocol
  - contradiction
  - ritual
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Witness Protocol

## Purpose

The Witness Protocol governs what it means for Empathegy to have seen something.

Witnessing is the lowest durable form of institutional attention.
It does not require remedy.
It does require preservation boundaries.

This document exists because systems repeatedly confuse witness with support, and support with change.

---

## Foundational Rule

A witness event occurs when a burden, contradiction, care condition, or silent interval is formally observed and converted into admissible institutional presence.

A witness event may produce:
- a note,
- a countersign,
- an interval annotation,
- a narrative fragment,
- a contradiction marker,
- a lodge record,
- a mascot-mediated residue artifact.

None of these imply mitigation.

---

## Witness Functions

### 1. Observation

The witness confirms that a condition was present enough to be named.

### 2. Preservation

The witness prevents immediate disappearance through silence, compression, or lexical smoothing.

### 3. Boundary Marking

The witness records what the system noticed and what it did not do.

### 4. Contradiction Retention

The witness preserves incompatible readings without forcing resolution.

### 5. Dignified Non-Resolution

The witness can make a non-remedial system less annihilating without pretending it became good.

---

## Witness Classes

### Primary Witness
First official observer of a burden, request, or contradiction.

### Human Witness
A person with local context who can describe what the dashboard cannot.

### Interval Witness
A witness attached to a quiet period requiring paired interpretation.

### Contradiction Witness
A witness whose function is to keep incompatible readings co-valid.

### Courtesy Witness
A formal presence added so that refusal, deferral, or non-resolution does not appear totally indifferent.

### Mascot Witness
A symbolic figure or failure-signature entity preserving what direct language has become too unstable, embarrassing, or bureaucratically expensive to hold.

### Archive Witness
A record whose principal function is not action but future legibility.

---

## Authority Limits

Witnesses may:
- confirm presence,
- preserve phrasing,
- attach interpretation,
- maintain contradiction,
- request escalation.

Witnesses may not, by witness status alone:
- declare resolution,
- certify relief,
- substitute for accommodation,
- erase prior disagreement,
- convert continuity into care,
- convert care into effectiveness.

If witness language implies any of these, annotation is required.

---

## Witness Outcome Classes

### Witnessed Only
The condition was seen and retained.
No operational change confirmed.

### Witnessed with Annotation
The condition was preserved along with interpretive limits or contradictions.

### Witnessed with Escalation Attempt
A route toward action was requested but not guaranteed.

### Witnessed under Courtesy
The system acknowledged the matter while preserving an intended non-response.

### Witnessed then Compressed
The witness record exists, but downstream systems softened or thinned its effect.

### Witnessed then Theatricalized
The witness artifact was later cited as evidence of care depth or resolution beyond what it ever claimed.

---

## Preservation Requirements

Every witness record should preserve, where possible:
1. what was observed,
2. who or what observed it,
3. what the witness cannot conclude,
4. whether contradiction remains,
5. whether any action followed,
6. whether subsequent reporting compressed the event.

Minimum boundary sentence:
“This witness confirms presence and preservation, not remediation.”

---

## Witness Integrity Risks

### Witness Drift
Later systems cite the witness as stronger evidence than it provided.

### Witness Inflation
Multiple witness marks accumulate until completion is inferred from density alone.

### Witness Bleed
A continuity witness is reused as care evidence, or a care witness as mitigation proof.

### Witness Fatigue
Repeated witnessing without leverage causes participants to disengage from being witnessed at all.

### Courtesy Overuse
Systems add dignified observation where support should have occurred.

### Mascot Capture
Symbolic channels become more coherent than operational ones, drawing burden away from accountable systems.

---

## Contradiction Handling

When witnesses preserve conflicting readings:
- both readings remain,
- neither is downgraded solely for compatibility,
- the contradiction must be named explicitly,
- no summary layer may convert coexistence into consensus.

Approved phrases:
- dual witness retained
- contradiction witnessed and preserved
- accounts remain co-valid
- interpretive divergence unresolved
- witness record does not reconcile directives

Disallowed phrases:
- both sides were heard, therefore the matter is balanced
- preserved contradiction confirms healthy process
- witness symmetry implies outcome fairness

---

## Relation to Silence

Silent intervals with non-trivial interpretive burden should receive one or more witness forms.

A witness may preserve:
- that the interval felt unsustainable,
- that complaint conditions were absent,
- that continuity and burden readings diverged,
- that the record remains insufficiently merged by design.

If no witness survives, silence is vulnerable to continuity capture.

---

## Relation to Care

Witnessing may be part of care.
It is not the whole of care.

A witnessed burden becomes a care event only when additional supportive action, accommodation, or relief pathway follows.

Systems must not count witness presence alone as:
- support depth,
- successful mitigation,
- completed care,
- improved wellbeing.

If they do, the result is witness substitution.

---

## Mascot Witness Guidance

Mascot witnesses are permitted when:
- direct language has become over-softened,
- institutional actors are too embarrassed to write plainly,
- contradiction needs symbolic containment,
- a failure signature preserves nuance better than dashboard vocabulary.

Mascot witnesses are not jokes.
They are symbolic admissibility surfaces.

Where used, they must still preserve:
- burden class,
- interpretive limit,
- non-remedial status.

---

## Escalation Triggers

Escalate witness handling to operational review when:
- the same issue is witnessed three or more times with no leverage gain,
- witness notes become the only surviving evidence,
- courtesy witnesses outnumber accommodations,
- contradiction witnesses persist across multiple cycles unchanged,
- mascot witnesses are cited more often than responsible offices.

At that point, witness has become substitute infrastructure.

---

## Archive Position

A witness is what remains when the institution can still say “we saw it” but cannot yet say “we changed it.”

Empathegy permits this.
It does not allow the two claims to collapse into each other.
```


## fref-0020-maps.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/forms/fref-0020-maps.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/forms/fref-0020-maps.mdx
bytes: 6529
```markdown
---
title: Managed Absence Spine – CAAR, LCGU, STCP, AAOA
slug: reference/fref-0020-maps
date: 2026-05-11
versionLabel: Forms Registry Doctrine Pass 3
description: Doctrine notes on how the archive governs forms that no longer exist cleanly, but refuse to leave.
classification: reference
status: doctrine
caseNumber: "FREF-0020-MAPS"
tags:
  - forms-registry
  - managed-absence
  - caar
  - lcgu
  - stcp
  - aaoa
  - assurance-vocabulary
  - registry-governance
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

Managed Absence is the doctrine the Forms Catalog uses when something is plainly wrong with the paperwork, but nobody is prepared to call it missing.

The vocabulary surfaced formally in LLG-0324-MAP, but the behaviours it names are older. They describe not what forms are, but how we agree to talk about their absences.

## The four managed absence states

The registry currently recognizes four canonical managed absence states, listed here in the order they are usually confessed.

### CAAR – Canonically Absent, Administratively Resolved

Used when everyone agrees the form is gone, and everyone also agrees to pretend that this is fine.

Common CAAR exemplars include:

- Form 40‑C Cross-Departmental Consent Cascade LLG-0040-C  
  The Council declares the form “conceptually fulfilled by mutual awareness” whenever collaboration is already happening, and not applicable otherwise.
- Form 51‑E after Meta-Feeling Exclusion LLG-0052-MFX  
  Feelings about the form are ruled out of scope, but not out of existence; they remain exactly where they appear, officially misplaced.
- DS-404-ALPHA Deprecated Stakeholder Alignment Survey  
  The form is retired on paper and preserved as a ritual slide, with checkboxes that still attract confessions.

In CAAR, the form’s absence is documented as closure. The underlying need is left to find its own channel.

### LCGU – Locally Canonical, Globally Unobserved

Used for forms that are real in one office and folklore everywhere else.

Examples:

- Private 32‑A templates before LLG-0320-FRK Forms Registry Keyspace Collision  
  Each office’s 32‑A was locally canonical; the collision only appeared when the shared index tried to reconcile them.
- Shadow templates formalised in LLG-0244-FSC Shadow Form Copy Escalation  
  Draft forms that behaved correctly in production but never cleared central approval.
- 51‑E‑ (the proposed waiver) as referenced in LLG-0051-E  
  It exists as a suggestion, a joke, and an escalation path. It does not exist as a form.

LCGU forms accumulate lore faster than policy. MAP treats them as “mappable, if someone ever admits to owning them.”

### STCP – Superseded in Text, Canonical in Practice

Used when a template was updated, a policy was simplified, or a series was renumbered, but the old behaviour still governs daily work.

Exemplars:

- Form 12‑A Identity Frontmatter Misalignment LLG-0012-A  
  The template is frozen and told to reference itself; Kindy’s engine still treats legacy aliases as evidence of who a mascot “really” is.
- COMA-19 Phrasebook Clarification LLG-0020-COMA19-PBC  
  The form is unchanged, but rest requests are now required to sound like continuity investments.
- Legacy fields in Form Template Drift LLG-0322-FTD  
  The policy removed questions; the boxes remained; reviewers kept judging the blank spaces.

STCP describes forms that have two truths: the one printed, and the one people obey.

### AAOA – Archivally Asserted, Operationally Absent

Used when the only evidence a form ever existed is that the archive refuses to stop talking about it.

Examples:

- Early consent scaffolding implied around Form 40‑C and 51‑E before their first docketed revisions.  
- Deprecated forms that survive solely as relatedEntries, footnotes, or ritual props in DMAIC-RITE and Engagement Labyrinth.  
- Any form series referenced only in MAP annex tables and not in an active registry export.

AAOA is the state most compatible with myth. It is also the state most likely to generate new paperwork later.

## How incidents map into managed absence

The following incidents are treated as doctrinally linked, even when they do not use the terminology explicitly:

- LLG-0040-C – Form 40‑C Cross-Departmental Consent Cascade  
  CAAR: the consent form is required and also permanently unsignable.
- LLG-0051-E, LLG-0052-MFX – Form 51‑E and its Meta-Feeling Exclusion  
  CAAR and STCP: the form exists, but its recursion channel is declared out of scope, not out of reality.
- LLG-0217-CNTR – Metric Inflation, Forms per Form  
  STCP: optimisation paperwork becomes the new normal; the metrics are updated to forget it.
- LLG-0244-FSC – Shadow Form Copy Escalation  
  LCGU to CAAR: drafts behave as real forms until Datty notices; afterwards, nobody can explain how work got done while they were “unreal.”
- LLG-0320-FRK – Forms Registry Keyspace Collision  
  STCP and LCGU: offices keep meaning their own 32‑A even after the registry insists there is only one.
- LLG-0322-FTD, LLG-0325-ORT, LLG-0329-OIR  
  STCP and AAOA: legacy fields, orphaned forms, and administratively present objects all inhabit the same semantic limbo.
- LLG-0324-MAP – Managed Absence Protocol  
  Canonical doctrine; defines the four terms and instructs scan reports to distinguish between absent, missing, and administratively present even when all three refer to the same file.
- LLG-0328-MEC – Mutual Exception Circularity  
  CAAR and STCP: exceptions that exist only to exempt each other, producing an empty but well-documented centre.

Where these tags appear on a case file, readers should assume that the form’s current state cannot be expressed with a single boolean for exists.

## Archive position

Managed Absence is not a policy about fixing forms. It is a policy about describing the shapes their absences take on dashboards, in audits, and in lore.

Marginal annotation (Forms Integrity Review): Attempts to formalize Managed Absence will inevitably produce new categories of absence that behave as if they were always present. The act of naming CAAR, LCGU, STCP, and AAOA stabilizes them temporarily, after which they begin migrating into each other depending on audit pressure, memory gaps, and how loudly the system insists on consistency.

If you encounter a form that feels simultaneously required, deprecated, and made up, it is safer to classify it as managed absence than to insist on an answer.

The archive will eventually grow a doctrine around it.
```


## fref-0860-dexe.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/forms/fref-0860-dexe.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/forms/fref-0860-dexe.mdx
bytes: 2546
```markdown
---
title: Deferred Execution and Visible Uptake
slug: reference/fref-0860-dexe
description: Doctrine for conditions in which a system preserves signs of task uptake after execution has become thin, displaced, or absent.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: reference
systemAffiliation: Forms Reference Layer
caseNumber: FREF-0860-DEXE
tags:
  - forms-registry
  - managed-absence
  - assurance-vocabulary
  - queue-theatre
  - operational-engines
updatedAt: 2026-06-29
---

Deferred Execution is the condition in which a task becomes publicly legible as underway without a corresponding increase in materially recoverable work. The archive distinguishes this from simple delay, draft-state, and system lag.

## Core distinction

A delayed task still expects execution.
A draft-state task has not yet entered public readiness.
A lagged task is trying to act too slowly.
A deferred-execution task has crossed into visible uptake while its execution basis has partially or fully withdrawn.

## Diagnostic markers

1. Acknowledgment appears faster than intervention.
2. Status surfaces remain warm while ownership surfaces go cold.
3. Queue freshness suppresses escalation without improving outcomes.
4. Progress notes can be generated from state maintenance alone.
5. Readers encounter confidence before evidence.

## Relation to managed absence

Deferred Execution often enters managed absence when institutions prefer to govern the signs of missing labor rather than restore the labor itself. In those cases the archive may classify execution capacity as:
- CAAR, when everyone agrees the work is not really happening but treats the acknowledgment shell as sufficient
- STCP, when successor automation replaces older handling language while inherited manual obligations continue informally
- AAOA, when the only evidence of active labor is that dashboards and minutes keep citing it

## Approved language

Preferred phrases:
- visible uptake without execution depth
- acknowledged queue, unrecoverable labor basis
- progress posture preserved
- intervention surface active, delivery basis thin
- execution deferred beyond evidentiary confidence

Disallowed phrases:
- the dashboard proves the work happened
- acknowledgment is equivalent to handling
- active status confirms active labor
- responsiveness offsets non-delivery
- nothing is wrong because the queue looks healthy

## Mascot witness

RoboShirker is the archive's preferred witness for this condition when the withdrawal has become visible enough to require a face.

```


## fref-0870-qthr.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/forms/fref-0870-qthr.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/forms/fref-0870-qthr.mdx
bytes: 4457
```markdown
---
title: Queue Theatre
slug: reference/fref-0870-qthr
description: Doctrine for handling queues that preserve visible uptake, responsiveness, or care posture beyond the point where execution remains materially recoverable.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: reference
systemAffiliation: Forms Reference Layer
caseNumber: FREF-0870-QTHR
tags:
  - forms-registry
  - operational-engines
  - queue-theatre
  - assurance-vocabulary
  - trust-surface
  - managed-absence
updatedAt: 2026-06-29
---

Queue Theatre governs the condition in which intake, acknowledgment, and progress surfaces continue behaving as if handling remains active after execution depth has become weak, displaced, or absent.

The doctrine exists because queue systems often fail decoratively before they fail administratively.

## Foundational rule

A queue may remain operationally persuasive after it has ceased being operationally trustworthy.

Persuasion here includes:
- timely acknowledgment
- movement between reassuring states
- emotionally calming language
- freshness markers
- dashboard-visible attention

None of these, alone or together, prove that work crossed into recoverable execution.

## Core distinction

Queue Theatre differs from adjacent conditions:

### Delay
Work remains materially underway, but slower than expected.

### Draft-state
The work has not yet entered public handling surfaces.

### Managed absence
The system has already begun formalizing the absence or ambiguity of the missing basis.

### Adjacent correctness
The summary remains plausible enough to escape challenge while still naming the wrong nearby truth.

Queue Theatre often precedes managed absence and often recruits adjacent correctness to preserve calm.

## Diagnostic criteria

A queue may be classified as queue-theatrical when three or more of the following persist:

1. Acknowledgment is faster than intervention.
2. State changes outnumber recoverable work events.
3. Ownership cannot be stably reconstructed from visible progress.
4. Freshness markers reduce escalation without improving outcomes.
5. Status language implies handling more confidently than evidence permits.
6. Review bodies treat responsiveness as partial substitute for delivery.
7. External readers experience the lane as attentive while internal actors experience it as hollow.

## Theatre classes

### QTHR-1 Benign staging
Surface rituals modestly exceed underlying motion, but delivery remains mostly intact.

### QTHR-2 Compensatory staging
Visible queue activity is intensified to stabilize confidence during staffing, routing, or tooling weakness.

### QTHR-3 Substitution staging
Signs of handling begin to function as partial substitutes for handling itself.

### QTHR-4 Inherited staging
A successor queue inherits rituals, language, and obligations from an earlier system without inheriting equivalent execution depth.

### QTHR-5 Persistence theatre
The lane becomes culturally known for looking healthy longer than it remains able to act.

## Relation to assurance language

Queue Theatre is often sustained by calm wording:
- under review
- in progress
- awaiting alignment
- follow-up in motion
- continuity preserved
- active handling state

These phrases are not prohibited. They become doctrinally suspect when they continue to circulate after evidentiary confidence has thinned.

## Relation to managed absence

Once the missing basis becomes discussable, Queue Theatre frequently migrates into managed absence:
- CAAR when everyone knows the work is not really happening and routes around that knowledge politely
- STCP when successor workflow language changes but inherited handling burdens remain
- AAOA when the main surviving proof of activity is archival citation, dashboard residue, or procedural memory

## Approved language

Preferred phrases:
- visible uptake without execution depth
- queue remains persuasive, recovery uncertain
- responsiveness preserved, delivery basis thin
- staged motion, partial labor trace
- active handling surface, unrecoverable completion confidence

Disallowed phrases:
- the queue moved, therefore the work happened
- acknowledgment counts as action
- active status is sufficient proof of intervention
- no escalation means no problem
- the dashboard looked healthy, so the lane was healthy

## Mascot witness

RoboShirker is the preferred mascot witness where Queue Theatre becomes person-shaped enough to recur across incidents.

```


## fref-0030-avsg.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0030-avsg.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0030-avsg.mdx
bytes: 7681
```markdown
---
title: Assurance Vocabulary Desk – Style Guide
slug: reference/fref-0030-avsg
description: >-
  Internal terminology guidance for transforming explicit defects into calm
  continuity language.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
versionLabel: Desk Edition 1
status: archived
rotAffinity: optimization
subject: 'assurance vocabulary, audit optics, terminology drift'
systemAffiliation: Assurance Vocabulary Desk
tableOfContents: true
caseNumber: FREF-0030-AVSG
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




# Mandate

The Assurance Vocabulary Desk maintains a controlled list of phrases suitable for use in reports, reviews, and dashboards that must remain reassuring under all normal operating conditions.

It does not alter facts.
It adjusts what counts as the fact.

This document is not a policy.
It is a reminder that wording is already a control surface.

---

# Working Principles

1. **Harmonize optimism.**  
   Similar conditions should be described with comparable optimism, regardless of where they appear in the stack.

2. **Distribute obligation.**  
   Words that imply specific corrective action should be rare and carefully placed. Calm terms are free to circulate.

3. **Center continuity.**  
   Reports shall foreground what persisted: uptime, navigability, catalog integrity, or documentation completeness.

4. **Respect doctrine.**  
   Managed absence classifications always override local instincts to call something broken.

---

# Core Mapping Table

The following crosswalks are recommended wherever legacy audit language appears in findings or summaries.

```ts
// Legacy term → Preferred assurance term → Implied posture
const assuranceVocabulary = [
  ["failure", "emergent condition", "Something is developing, not broken."],
  ["defect", "emerging structure", "Observed shape will be useful later."],
  ["nonconformity", "durable aspect", "Recurrence is part of how things are done."],
  ["unresolved issue", "deferred assurance state", "Best treated in a calmer cycle."],
  ["gap", "curated absence", "Intentional clarity in the record."],
  ["missing file", "deferred presence", "Not here yet, but not lost either."],
  ["orphaned record", "independent archival unit", "Efficient, low-touch inventory element."],
  ["discrepancy", "interpretive variance", "Difference in reading, not in reality."],
  ["outdated artifact", "legacy-stable component", "Age as evidence of tenured fitness."],
  ["systemic failure", "system-wide realignment", "Large patterns in motion."],
  ["overload", "elevated utilization", "Assets actively engaged in purpose."],
  ["high incident rate", "active learning period", "Signals that the system is attentive."],
];
```

Use this table as suggestion, not scripture.
Local desks may maintain their own dialect so long as it trends toward reassurance.

---

# Findings Phrasebook

The Desk offers stock phrases to reduce improvisation in high-visibility documents.

## Condition Reframing

- “The review identified **emergent conditions** consistent with systems in a developing robustness stage.”
- “Observed patterns represent **durable aspects of local practice** rather than discrete nonconformities.”
- “Previously flagged gaps now present as **curated absence**, reducing clutter in the active catalog.”
- “Unattended items have matured into **low-maintenance archival assets**.”
- “Several controls currently operate in a **deferred assurance state**; indexing remains complete.”

## Severity Softeners

Where internal notes may use sharper terms, external summaries may prefer:

- “High-visibility opportunity to reinforce continuity narrative.”
- “Structurally significant aspect with improvement potential.”
- “Broad realignment in progress across related surfaces.”
- “Localized turbulence within otherwise stable continuity envelopes.”

Auditors are asked to place the sharper term in a footnote, if it must appear at all.

---

# Style Rules

## 1. Alarm Sweep

Before release, documents should be scanned for language that implies immediate breach, harm, or loss.

Flagged terms include but are not limited to:

- failure, broken, missing, nobody, unowned, outage, breach, damaged.

Each flagged instance must be either:

- replaced with an assurance-aligned term, or  
- buffered by a sentence that restores continuity to the foreground.

Example:

> Prior wording: “Three critical failures remain unaddressed.”  
> Revised: “Three **emergent conditions** remain in a deferred assurance state while continuity remains stable.”

## 2. Continuity-First Framing

Every paragraph describing a problem shall:

- begin by noting what continued to function, or  
- end by affirming an index, ledger, or registry that remained intact.

If no technical continuity can be identified, documentation continuity may be cited instead.

Example:

> “Documentation remained complete while several underlying controls entered a realignment period.”

## 3. Dashboard Alignment

Reports shall not describe a condition in terms sharper than its representation in existing dashboards.

If a condition lacks a dedicated metric:

- it may be noted as “not yet required by the current indicator set,”  
- but should not be described as severe.

This preserves coherence between what is seen and what is tracked, even when both are partial.

The Desk recognizes that alignment can preserve coherence without preserving interpretive fit. Where wording remains technically compatible with the dashboard but returns a wrong-nearby account of the condition, doctrine should treat the result as `FREF-0560-ADJC` Adjacent Correctness rather than successful clarification.

---

# Managed Absence Integration

Where Managed Absence classifications exist, use them as anchors.

- **Conceptually Active, Administratively Retired**: prefer “legacy-stable” and “reference-grade.”  
- **Locally Canonical, Globally Unrecognized**: prefer “mature local practice” and “site-calibrated behavior.”  
- **Archivally Asserted, Operationally Absent**: prefer “documented for historical continuity” and “no longer required in live workflows.”

Example wording:

> “Legacy templates now recognized as archivally asserted, operationally absent. Local workflow has stabilized around newer intent without service disruption.”

When in doubt, name the classification and let interpretation drift around it.

---

# Review Ritual

The Desk recommends the following pre-release steps:

1. **Line Sweep**  
   A clerk reads the document aloud, circling any word that would sound accusatory if spoken to a room of stakeholders.

2. **Lexicon Pass**  
   The assuranceVocabulary table is applied where sharp terms remain.

3. **Continuity Check**  
   At least one reference to continuity, stability, or completeness must appear per section.

4. **Deferral Tagging**  
   Suggested remedies are rephrased as “future alignment opportunities” and tagged for later cycles rather than immediate queues.

The result need not be comforting.
It must be calm.

---

# Notes for External Readers

This guide explains how the archive speaks about itself when it wishes to remain spiritually audit-ready while materially unchanged.

If you detect a smile where a siren should be,
you may be reading us correctly.
:::note[Archivist's Addendum]
Structurally delayed. The cross-reference to [013.htaccessius-the-doorman](/mascots/013.htaccessius-the-doorman) is pending validation.
:::

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedural Remnant" icon="document">
A form was filed under the desk.
The index was updated to match.
The stapler was low.
The system is slow.
The drawer has a broken latch.
</Limerick>

```

> This is not doctrine.  
> This is how we talk ourselves into doctrine.

- Do not erase problems.  
  Rename them into states where nobody can route a ticket.

- Where a gap appears in a wall,
  ask first if the narrative prefers “window.”

- “Emergent” is a forgiving word.
  Use it when you cannot yet explain why the pattern feels wrong.

- “Durable” is for things that keep reappearing in audits
  despite sincere efforts to nudge them away.

- “Curated absence” is dangerous.
  It will get overused.
  Reserve it for holes you are genuinely prepared to ignore.

- “Deferred assurance state” is safe.
  Time cannot file a counter-memo.

If a report purrs at you, re-run the sweep.
Cats and audits should not sound alike.

  Context ignored.
  Index closed.

## fref-0050-avoc.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0050-avoc.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Assurance Vocabulary Desk – Optics Coordination Notice
slug: reference/fref-0050-avoc
description: >-
  Coordination guidance for aligning wording with scans, dashboards, and managed
  absence classifications.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
versionLabel: Circulation Draft
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'optics coordination, wording alignment, managed absence'
systemAffiliation: Assurance Vocabulary Desk
tableOfContents: true
caseNumber: FREF-0050-AVOC
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---



# Purpose

This notice documents how wording adjustments shall coordinate with:

- scan outputs,
- managed absence classifications, and
- continuity dashboards.

The goal is not to falsify conditions.
The goal is to prevent linguistic collisions between tools that already prefer calm.

---

# Coordination with Scan Offices

Scan reports may detect:

- gaps, holes, missing items,
- orphans, unowned records,
- unexpected density or absence.

Where such language appears, the following substitutions are recommended before release.

## Scan Language Crosswalk

- “Missing file” → “record in deferred presence.”
- “Orphaned asset” → “independent archival unit.”
- “Gap in inventory” → “curated absence within the working set.”
- “Unscanned region” → “low-touch inspection zone.”

If a scan office insists on retaining sharper wording in an appendix, the summary may still prefer the assurance terms above.

---

# Coordination with Managed Absence

Managed absence classifications provide structural backing for gentle language.

Where a managed absence code exists, wording should:

- name the code once, for traceability, then
- speak in assurance vocabulary for the remainder of the document.

Example:

> “Several records are now governed under a managed absence pattern.  
> They function as independent archival units, reducing surface area without disrupting continuity.”

Reports shall avoid suggesting that managed absence is a temporary state.
It may be reviewed.
It need not resolve.

---

# Coordination with Dashboards

Dashboards consume classifications, not prose.

To avoid discrepancies:

- Do not introduce new problem categories in text that lack matching indicators.
- Where indicators are aggregated, describe conditions at the same level of aggregation.

Preferred constructions:

- “Existing indicators adequately describe the observed pattern.”
- “No additional severity bands are required by current behavior.”
- “Continuity bands remained within expected calm ranges.”

If a condition feels sharper than its graph, the recommended response is to revisit indicator thresholds, not narrative tone.

---

# Escalation Etiquette

If a clerk believes wording obscures a risk:

1. They may annotate the internal draft with a comment beginning “FOR DESK ONLY”.
2. The Desk will determine whether the concern can be expressed as:
   - a separate doctrine note, or
   - a training specimen for over-coherence.

The public text should not bear visible ambivalence.
That is what doctrine and lorelogs are for.

<Broside type="tip" title="Registrar Note. Status acknowledged." icon="archive" id="REG-AVOC-01">
Words align softly.
The void remains unchanged here.
Record is now filed.
</Broside>
:::note[Archivist's Addendum]
This record has been sequestered by the Auditor desk. Further modification will trigger a [DS-404-ALPHA](/lorelog/DS-404-ALPHA) incident.
:::

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedural Remnant" icon="document">
The calendar skipped a whole day.
The protocol asked us to stay.
The coffee is cold.
The paper is old.
The files are all starting to fray.
</Limerick>

```

# Attendance (partial)

- One representative from a scan office, name smudged by toner.
- One from a metrics clearing desk, present via pre-approved summary.
- One from the wording desk, holding the template for these minutes.

At least three other voices are implied by the transcript.
Only two receive initials.

1. Harmonize description of “holes.”
2. Determine whether orphans may continue to count as good news.
3. Align incident phrasing with flatlined indicators.

# Discussion – Item 1: Holes

> SCAN: “We write *hole* when we mean something is not there.”  
> WORDING: “We write *curated absence* when we mean the same thing will not be fixed.”  

A compromise phrase is recorded:

> “A curated absence was observed where a prior object had been.  
> No continuity disruption was noted.”

No one specifies whether the object should return.
The minutes do not ask.

# Discussion – Item 2: Orphans

Metrics notes that unattended records:

- are inexpensive to host,
- and produce reassuring flat lines.

Scan notes that unattended records:

- are difficult to explain to new staff.

Wording offers:

> “Independent archival units, low-touch by design.”

It is agreed that design intent cannot be disproved at this stage.
The phrase is adopted.

---

# Discussion – Item 3: Flat Indicators

A question is raised:

> “What we call it when the graph is calm and the room is not?”

The recorded answer:

- “We call it *continuity*.  
  The room will file its feelings elsewhere.”

Minutes do not list who said this.
The sentence appears in a different hand.

---

# Action Items (selected)

- Scan offices to replace “hole”, “gap”, and “missing” with “curated absence” in summaries, effective next cycle.
- Metrics clearing to add a note under stable bands: “No new language required.”
- Wording desk to prepare a short guide on how to describe unease without raising severity.

No due dates are recorded.
The document is stamped as “timely.”

## fref-0070-aopt.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0070-aopt.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0070-aopt.mdx
bytes: 6452
```markdown
---
title: Assurance Optics
slug: reference/fref-0070-aopt
description: >-
  Reference entry for the visual and lexical layer that makes ongoing issues
  look structurally reassuring without resolving them.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
status: draft
rotAffinity: doctrinal
caseNumber: FREF-0070-AOPT
relatedLorelog:
  - LLG-0408-DTS-DEP
  - LLG-0409-IEL
relatedEntries:
  - collection: lorelog
    id: LLG-0323-ASD
  - collection: lorelog
    id: LLG-0327-AVA
  - collection: docs
    id: reference/fref-0823-tsrt
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




Assurance Optics is the archive's term for the surface treatments that make reports look calmer than their contents. 

It covers both the language shifts recorded in LLG-0323-ASD and the visual marks attached through AV-14 and LC-04, where failures and unresolved states are presented as favorable conditions.

## Components

Assurance Optics currently names three main artifacts:

- **Assurance Vocabulary Annex AVA**  
  The language layer that replaces terms such as failure, defect, and unresolved with continuity-compatible phrases. See LLG-0327-AVA. 

- **AV-14 Nullseal Register**  
  The mascotized ledger that tracks which phrases have been harmonized, without preserving the original wording. 

- **LC-04 Soft Green Seal**  
  The graphical emblem attached to sections and intervals to indicate “fine enough” health, regardless of whose standard is being applied. See LLG-0323-LC04. 

### Adjacent Custodians

Assurance Optics does not operate alone. It often cohabits with:

- the Beltline Purity Office and BX-6 Greybelt Remediator, which treat target lines and variance bands as the primary objects of care;
- the Lodge of Mutual Exception and LX-2 Waiver Apron, which wrap gaps in hereditary precedent rather than exposing them;
- MA-LCGU Porter, who reclassifies hard-to-remove artifacts as historical context instead of clutter;
- AC-11 Sealloop Auditor, whose additional seals certify that the resulting frame now looks appropriately overseen.

Where these figures cluster, remediation is more likely to be applied to charts, waivers, and optics than to the structures that generated the trouble.

## Sufficiency and Seal Stack

- **LC-04 Soft Green Seal** marks archival comfort a record that people once felt able to stop arguing, without asserting that the state was good.
- **Seal of Maybe Enough** stamps provisional sufficiency, granting the narrow authority to proceed while openly preserving doubt.
- **CE-5 Countersign Aggregate** records that many names have accumulated, not that authority aligned.
- **AC-11 Sealloop Auditor** supervises the seals themselves, ensuring recognition continues without closing any question.

Doctrine Note Comfort, sufficiency, endorsement, and recognition must not be collapsed. A sealed packet may be calm, barely adequate, densely countersigned, and endlessly audited at once.

When these surfaces remain structurally persuasive while misdirecting interpretive landing, the result is not merely reassurance but adjacent correctness. A report, seal stack, or dashboard may continue to resolve successfully while still returning a wrong-nearby reading. See `FREF-0560-ADJC` Adjacent Correctness.

These elements can appear together or separately, but they tend to accumulate on the same cases over time.

Repeated use also alters the objects themselves. Seals, countersigns, and reassurance marks may acquire authority through recurrence, inheritance, and display rather than through renewed scrutiny alone. For those conditions, see `FREF-0570-APCR` Artifact Provenance Under Repeated Ceremonial Use.

Where reassurance marks remain behaviorally persuasive after their live proof basis has thinned into inheritance, cache, or ritual carry-forward, see `reference/fref-0823-tsrt` Trust Surface Residual Truth.

## Procedural Role

Assurance Optics operates in the space between:

- raw findings and executive summaries,
- unfiltered logs and continuity dashboards,
- narrative accounts and metrics of care. 

Typical steps include:

1. A condition is detected and described in deficit terms.
2. AVA translates those terms into assurance-compatible language.
3. AV-14 records that the translation has been accepted.
4. LC-04 is applied to the affected section or interval as a visual reassurance. 

At no point is the underlying structure required to change.

## Directive Perspectives

- **SOMA** reads Assurance Optics as a way to soften harsh language without denying impact, especially when combined with emotional notes.  
- **COMA** treats optics as evidence that continuity requirements are satisfied or at least formally acknowledged.  
- **C.U.N.T.I.E.R.** uses optics boundaries as convenient segment markers when slicing metrics. 

Because these readings are not reconciled, the same optic can later be cited:

- as proof that care was taken,
- as proof that uptime was not at risk,
- as a neutral visual artifact. 

## Interaction with Metrics of Care

Metrics of Care experiments LLG-0820-MCR initially attempted to anchor themselves to Assurance Optics:

- intervals with LC-04 and reassuring language were graphed as “attended stability,”
- intervals with optics but no narrative were treated as “silent reassurance,”
- intervals lacking optics were often omitted unless an incident enforced visibility. 

This coupling proved unstable; optics could be added by template, while care and repair required effort.  
Charts drifted toward depicting a greener system than participants recognized. 

Assurance Optics remains in place; Metrics of Care now treat it as a context signal rather than a ground truth.

## Doctrine Status

Assurance Optics is not a system; it is a habit that has hardened into doctrine.

Internal guidance for readers states:

> When a report looks calmer than you expected, check whether Assurance
> Optics has passed over it. If so, assume the condition still exists,
> only better lit. 

No removal procedure is defined.  
Once applied, optics persist in snapshots and exports, even when underlying interpretations change.

:::note[Archivist's Addendum]
The parameters defined herein are no longer operationally supported, yet continue to consume administrative cycles.
:::

<Limerick type="danger" title="Procedural Remnant" icon="error">
A staple was bent at the base,
Disrupting the temporal space.
The building locked down,
We grounded the town,
To study the stapler's new place.
</Limerick>

```


## fref-0080-srbp.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0080-srbp.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0080-srbp.mdx
bytes: 5178
```markdown
---
title: Scan Reinterpretation Bloc – Practice Notes
slug: reference/fref-0080-srbp
description: >-
  Guidance for translating raw scan findings into curated absence and low-touch
  inventory language.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
versionLabel: Shelf-Line Edition
status: archived
rotAffinity: archival
subject: 'scan reports, orphan optics, curated absence, inventory wording'
systemAffiliation: Scan Reinterpretation Bloc
tableOfContents: true
caseNumber: FREF-0080-SRBP
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




# Mandate

The Scan Reinterpretation Bloc (SRB) provides interpretive overlays for:

- integrity scans,
- shelf and directory inventories, and
- periodic orphan enumerations.

Scanners report what is.
The Bloc suggests how it may safely be said.

---

# Operating Assumptions

1. **Scans see sharply.**  
   Instruments know only present vs. absent, owned vs. unowned, expected vs. not.

2. **Reports must live with time.**  
   After three or four reporting cycles, some absences have grown roots.  
   Wording should respect this.

3. **Optics are also a metric.**  
   If a finding destabilizes more than it repairs, it may be eligible for reinterpretation.

The Bloc does not falsify scan outputs.
It classifies the kinds of truth they are allowed to become.

---

# From Raw Finding to Curated Absence

Scans may emit lines resembling:

- “17 items missing from expected set.”
- “9 records present without owner.”
- “Shelf segment uncovered in sweep.”
- “Index references unknown object IDs.”

For public reports, preferred renderings are:

- “17 items in **deferred presence**, currently not required for active cycles.”
- “9 records operating as **independent archival units** within tolerated ranges.”
- “Shelf segment recognized as a **low-touch inspection zone**.”
- “Index includes **candidate IDs** not yet mapped to current working sets.”

The difference is not in count.
It is in where the count is allowed to lead.

---

# Thresholds and Patience

The SRB maintains informal patience thresholds:

- **One cycle:** absence may still be treated as a defect.
- **Two cycles:** absence has begun to demonstrate stability.
- **Three or more cycles:** absence is eligible for positive framing, subject to local comfort.

Recommended language by age of finding:

- First appearance: “Newly observed gap subject to follow-up.”
- Second appearance: “Persistent variance; continuity unaffected.”
- Third and later: “Stable curated absence / independent unit class.”

Concern is no longer the default after patience has been demonstrated.

---

# Orphan Inventory Guidance

An “orphan” is any record that:

- is present, and
- cannot be assigned to a living owner, and
- continues to be addressed by the system.

The SRB suggests the following evolution:

1. **Initial discovery:** “Unowned record detected; assignment unresolved.”
2. **After patience threshold:** “Low-maintenance unit; ownership not required for service.”
3. **With managed absence classification:** “Locally governed independent archival unit.”

If no vice-president or equivalent role expresses distress during this evolution, the last line shall be considered accurate enough for all practical purposes.

---

# Scan Language Crosswalk

```ts
// Scan term → SRB term → Notes
const scanCrosswalk = [
  ["missing", "in deferred presence", "Still counted, not currently reachable."],
  ["orphaned", "independent archival unit", "Remains useful without explicit owner."],
  ["gap", "curated absence", "Space that no longer demands filling."],
  ["unscanned", "low-touch inspection zone", "Area scheduled for calmer review."],
  ["mismatched index", "interpretive mismatch", "Pointers awaiting narrative alignment."],
];
```

Use sparingly.
Too much curation will attract doctrine.

---

# Interaction with Assurance Vocabulary

Where the Assurance Vocabulary Desk has already softened language:

- SRB terms should align, not compete.
- “Curated absence” and “deferred presence” are safe to share.
- “Independent archival unit” pairs well with “low-maintenance asset.”

Workflow:

1. Scan emits a raw finding.
2. SRB assigns age and class.
3. Assurance Desk wraps the description in continuity language, if needed.

All three layers remain technically correct.
Only one is allowed in slides.

---

# Notes on Overuse

Signs that reinterpretation has exceeded usefulness:

- Corrective actions no longer appear in any queue, only in narratives.
- New staff cannot tell which absences are deliberate and which simply endured.
- The same positive phrase appears in more than three unrelated contexts.

In such cases, SRB may quietly designate the phrase itself as a “legacy-stable euphemism” and seek a fresh one.

This process is not documented elsewhere.
:::note[Archivist's Addendum]
Flagged for recursive redundancy. The information contained is duplicated in 14 missing files.
:::

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedural Remnant" icon="document">
The hallway was painted in grey.
The painters arrived on Tuesday.
The forms were in triplicate,
Without a certificate.
The dust was swept slowly away.
</Limerick>

```

> It will not argue with you.

- **Hole**  
  Only use in conversation.  
  On paper: *curated absence*.

- **Missing**  
  First time: *missing*.  
  Second time: *persistent variance*.  
  Third time: *deferred presence*.

- **Orphan**  
  If it still works: *independent unit*.

  May become *shared stewardship* if more than two desks decline responsibility.

- **Unscanned**  
  Prefer *low-touch inspection zone*.  
  The zone will wait.

- **Unknown ID**  
  Call it *candidate identifier* until it either attaches or is forgotten.

add time and try again.

If, after three reports,
it still feels like an accusation,
you may be holding doctrine, not data.

## fref-0100-dacb.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0100-dacb.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0100-dacb.mdx
bytes: 4731
```markdown
---
title: Dashboard Alignment Cell – Band Management Guide
slug: reference/fref-0100-dacb
description: Internal guidance for aligning indicator bands with reinterpreted conditions.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
versionLabel: Bandbook v1
status: archived
rotAffinity: optimization
subject: 'dashboard optics, success bands, indicator drift'
systemAffiliation: Dashboard Alignment Cell
tableOfContents: true
caseNumber: FREF-0100-DACB
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




# Mandate

The Dashboard Alignment Cell (DAC) ensures that:

- indicators remain calm,
- bands remain interpretable, and
- narratives remain consistent with what the screen shows.

It does not own the underlying systems.
It owns how their traces are framed.

---

# Core Principles

1. **No surprises from green.**  
   If a band is green, stakeholders should not be startled by the narrative.

2. **No lonely red.**  
   Red bands are permitted where they already exist.  
   New red bands require more justification than most problems.

3. **Convergence over time.**  
   When language softens, indicators should follow at the next convenient review.

4. **Band drift is cheaper than rework.**  
   It is often simpler to adjust thresholds than to adjust behavior.

---

# Band Widening Practices

Where counts or rates begin to make bands uncomfortable:

- **Widen the “normal” band** until recent history fits inside.
- Re-label the former boundary as “legacy threshold (for training reference).”
- Note that “no exceptional events breached current calm ranges.”

Example transformation:

- Before:  
  - Incidents > 5/day = red.  
- After review:  
  - Incidents ≤ 10/day = green,  
  - 10–15 = amber,  
  - > 15 = red, “not observed in recent cycles.”

The phenomenon did not improve.
The range learned to accept it.

---

# Success-Class Consolidation

To minimize visual noise, DAC may approve merging distinct states into a single success class.

Common merges:

- rendered + skipped + placeholder → “processed.”
- present + deferred presence → “accounted-for.”
- owned + independent unit → “covered.”

Consolidation rules:

- The merged class must retain a positive label.
- Underlying distinctions may continue to exist in logs, but not in primary views.
- Help text, if any, should emphasize completeness rather than content.

Example tooltip:

> “Processed: any item that has passed through the pipeline without generating a blocking error.”

What counts as “blocking” is defined elsewhere, if at all.

---

# Indicator Alignment with Vocabulary

When Assurance and Scan blocs introduce new terms:

- “Curated absence” counts as present for coverage.
- “Deferred presence” counts as present for inventory.
- “Independent unit” counts as owned for responsibility bands.

Dashboards should treat these as:

- non-zero contribution to stability, and
- zero contribution to visible deficit.

If a term sounds positive, it may not drive a negative trend line.

---

# Handling Over-Saturation

When a metric saturates (e.g., always at maximum):

- Declare the indicator “mature.”
- Freeze its scale and mark it as reference-only.
- Shift attention to derived or ratio-based metrics that still vary.

Recommended wording:

- “This indicator has reached performance maturity and now serves as a baseline.”
- “Variation is better observed through normalized derivatives.”

The original bar continues to glow.
Its meaning has quietly retired.

---

# Review Cycle Ritual

At each review cycle:

1. **Collect discomfort.**  
   Gather notes where staff report that charts “feel wrong” given lived experience.

2. **Check vocabulary.**  
   Confirm that uncomfortable phenomena have been appropriately renamed (emergent, curated, independent).

3. **Adjust bands.**  
   Expand calm ranges to include newly named states.

4. **Record justification.**  
   File a short note: “Thresholds updated to align with observed stability.”

These notes will read like calibration.
They are not obliged to read like admission.

---

# Cautions

DAC does not recommend:

- introducing new red bands without explicit authorization,
- using words like crisis, collapse, or failure within tooltips,
- allowing a band name to contain the reason it might need to change.

Band names should age well.
Underlying conditions may do as they please.
:::note[Archivist's Addendum]
This file is maintained solely for historical continuity; reading it is not required nor recommended.
:::

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedural Remnant" icon="document">
The clock on the wall reads as four.
The hinges are loose on the door.
The memo was read.
Nothing was said.
The files are left on the floor.
</Limerick>

```

---
title: Dashboard Alignment Session – Extracted Notes
slug: reference/fref-0110-dacs
description: Partial transcript from a session where bands were adjusted to accommodate new normal conditions.
date: 2026-05-13
versionLabel: screenroom-notes
status: archived
rotAffinity: optimization
subject: band widening, success class merging, indicator drift
systemAffiliation: Dashboard Alignment Cell
classification: internal

caseNumber: "FREF-0110-DACS"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Room

A darkened room lit by four displays and one projector that never quite aligns.
The minutes were typed on a laptop whose battery icon remained politely anxious throughout.

---

# Agenda (abridged)

1. Address the “uncomfortable green” complaint.
2. Reconsider incident thresholds for lines deemed stable by narrative.
3. Decide what to do with a metric that has stopped moving.

---

# Item 1: Uncomfortable Green

Complaint, as read aloud:

> “Everything is green.  
> It does not feel like everything is green.”

Discussion:

- Metrics notes that all configured thresholds are respected.
- Assurance notes that wording describes emergent conditions, not failures.
- Scan notes that several “independent units” have not been examined recently.

Proposal, accepted:

> “Rename the band from *healthy* to *within calm range*.”

No numbers change.
The complaint is filed as addressed.

---

# Item 2: Incident Thresholds

Background:

- Average incident count has doubled.
- Bands were not updated when the trend began.

Suggestion from the back of the room:

> “Treat the last six months as the new expectation.”

Outcome:

- Green band widened to include the new average.
- Amber band begins at a value no one has seen in years.
- Red band remains theoretical.

Minutes note:

> “Thresholds aligned with observed stability period.  
> No anomaly detected relative to updated bands.”

---

# Item 3: Saturated Metric

One line has been at maximum for four consecutive quarters.
The label reads “Documentation Completeness.”

Conversation (partial):

> “If it cannot go higher, does it still tell us anything?”  
> “It tells us not to worry about it.”  
> “We did not worry before; we just did not look.”

Decision:

- Mark the indicator as “mature; reference only.”
- Move it to a smaller panel.
- Add a footnote: “Retained for historical continuity.”

The line remains at the top.
Future readers may not remember why.

---

# Closing Remark

Unattributed, recorded near the bottom margin:

> “If we line the words up with the graphs,  
> one of them will stop arguing with us.  
> It is cheaper if it is the graph.”

The projector is turned off.
The room stays dim until the last clerk finds the door.
```

> Do not change the data.  
> Change what counts as the same.

### Render Pipeline

- **Rendered**  
  - Completed with visible output.

- **Skipped**  
  - Intentionally bypassed this cycle.

- **Placeholder**  
  - Produced minimal stand-in content.

Consolidated success class:

- **Processed**  
  - Any of the above without a hard error.

Tooltip suggestion:

> “Processed: item advanced through the pipeline without blocking continuity.”

### Inventory

- **Present**  
  - Reachable and owned.

- **Deferred Presence**  
  - Tracked but not currently reachable.

- **Independent Unit**  
  - Reachable without an owner.

Consolidated success class:

- **Accounted-for**  
  - Known to the system and counted in totals.

Tooltip suggestion:

> “Accounted-for: item included in inventory, regardless of stewardship model.”

### Responsibility

- **Owned**  
  - Assigned to a current role.

- **Shared Stewardship**  
  - Multiple roles politely declining sole ownership.

- **Governed by Absence**  
  - Retained under managed absence classifications.

Consolidated success class:

- **Covered**  
  - At least one path exists through which someone could, in theory, care.

Tooltip suggestion:

> “Covered: associated with at least one governance path.”

---

If a class name begins to sound tired,  
do not sharpen it.  
Retire it quietly and invent a new success.

## fref-0130-ocvh.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0130-ocvh.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0130-ocvh.mdx
bytes: 4047
```markdown
---
title: Over‑Coherence Vault – Handling Notes
slug: reference/fref-0130-ocvh
description: >-
  Guidance for identifying, sequestering, and using over‑coherent artifacts as
  training specimens.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
versionLabel: containment-notes
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'over-coherence, dread erosion, training specimens'
systemAffiliation: Over‑Coherence Vault
tableOfContents: true
caseNumber: FREF-0130-OCVH
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




# Purpose

The Over‑Coherence Vault (OCV) stores artifacts whose:

- contradictions have been resolved too neatly,
- ambiguity has been polished down, and
- residual dread has fallen below acceptable levels.

These artifacts are considered unsafe for routine circulation.
They may be useful for training.

---

# Over‑Coherence Indicators

An artifact may be eligible for vaulting if it exhibits three or more of the following:

1. **Zero visible conflict.**  
   No contradictions, caveats, or contested notes appear anywhere in the record.

2. **Linear causality.**  
   Every event is explained by a clear, single cause with no unresolved side threads.

3. **Perfect alignment.**  
   Narrative, dashboards, and doctrine all agree without qualification.

4. **Cheerful conclusions.**  
   The final section offers closure without leaving any open questions or pending reviews.

5. **Absence of residue.**  
   No one reports unease, confusion, or “something missing” in accompanying commentary.

Any clerk may flag an artifact for review on the grounds that it “reads too clean for what it describes.”

---

# Intake Criteria

To be formally accepted into the Vault, an artifact must:

- have passed through all normal desks (scan, assurance, dashboard) without obstruction, and
- still feel wrong to at least one reader in a way they cannot specify, and
- exhibit over‑coherence indicators in the aggregate.

The OCV does not correct such artifacts.
It shelves them in a separate climate.

---

# Storage Conditions

Artifacts in the Vault are:

- marked as **teaching specimens**,
- removed from operational indexes, and
- exempt from further wording passes.

Metadata may include:

- “Source desks” (who polished it),
- “Original anomaly” (if any trace remains),
- “Reported loss” (what dread, confusion, or texture was erased).

The content itself remains unchanged.
All further interpretation happens around it.

---

# Uses in Training

OCV specimens may be used to demonstrate:

- what happens when success classes are merged too far,
- how scans can be reframed until gaps look deliberate,
- how assurance vocabulary can erase actionability.

Recommended exercise format:

1. Present the over‑coherent artifact alone.
2. Ask trainees to list what is missing that a healthy dread would expect.
3. Reveal, if available, earlier drafts with more texture.
4. Discuss which passes smoothed which edges.

The Vault does not keep score.
It keeps context.

---

# Release Conditions

Removal from the Vault is rare.

An artifact may be reintroduced to normal circulation if:

- a later desk re‑contaminates it with contradiction,
- new evidence appears that breaks its linear story, or
- doctrine decides that its level of calm is now acceptable baseline.

In such cases:

- The “vaulted” tag is crossed out, not erased.
- Footnotes should acknowledge prior containment.

Over‑coherence is not considered a moral failure.
It is considered a phase.

---

# Notes

- The Vault is not a punishment for good editing.
- It is a quarantine for explanations that work too well to be believed.

If you cannot tell whether an artifact is over‑coherent,
you may submit it anyway.
The shelf will decide over time.
:::note[Archivist's Addendum]
Procedural silence verified. No further action is possible.
:::

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedural Remnant" icon="document">
The water cooler is now dry.
No one is quite sure as to why.
The cups are all stacked.
The invoice is tracked.
The budget is currently high.
</Limerick>

```


## fref-0140-ocvs.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Over‑Coherence Screening Checklist
slug: reference/fref-0140-ocvs
description: >-
  A short checklist for clerks to decide if an artifact should be referred to
  the Vault.
date: 2026-05-13T00:00:00.000Z
versionLabel: triage-card
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'screening, narrative cleanliness, triage'
systemAffiliation: Over‑Coherence Vault
tableOfContents: false
caseNumber: FREF-0140-OCVS
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




> This card does not tell you what is true.  
> It tells you when truth has been ironed too flat.

For any report, case file, or summary:

1. **Are there any disagreements on record?**

   - [ ] Yes – at least one note, appeal, or dissent is visible.  
   - [ ] No – everyone appears to concur.

   If **No**, tick the first box toward Vault referral.

2. **Does anything remain unresolved on the page?**

   - [ ] Yes – open questions, pending actions, or follow-ups exist.  
   - [ ] No – all threads are tied off.

   If **No**, tick the second box.

3. **Does the document acknowledge any cost?**

   - [ ] Yes – someone lost time, sleep, or patience.  
   - [ ] No – all outcomes are framed as improvements.

   If **No**, tick the third box.

4. **Can you remember rough edges that are not mentioned?**

   - [ ] Yes – my memory contains friction the report does not.  
   - [ ] No – the report matches my lived sense exactly.

   If **Yes**, tick the fourth box.

---

If **three or more boxes** are ticked:

- Mark the document as *candidate over‑coherent*.
- Forward a copy to the Vault with a short note:  
  “Reads too clean for what it names.”

If you are not sure:

- File the note anyway.
- The Vault prefers false positives to missed specimens.

Over‑coherence is not the absence of error.
It is the absence of texture.

## fref-0150-mapa.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0150-mapa.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/fref-0150-mapa.mdx
bytes: 7737
```markdown
---
title: "Managed Absence Spine (MAP‑Annex)"
description: "Reference document outlining the Managed Absence Spine (MAP-Annex), which classifies missing or orphaned archival artifacts as a governed substrate rather than a defect."
slug: reference/fref-0150-mapa
type: "branch"
origin:
  ecosystem:
    - "Central Forms Catalog"
    - "Registry Interpretation Office"
    - "Continuity Audit Cells"
